Draining,\n48\t    /// Node has failed (unplanned outage).\n49\t    Failed,\n50\t    /// Node has been removed from the cluster (tracked for migration).\n51\t    Removed,\n52\t}\n53\t\n54\timpl NodeStatus {\n55\t    /// Check if a transition from `self` to `new_status` is valid.\n56\t    ///\n57\t    /// # State Transition Rules\n58\t    ///\n59\t    /// | From | To | Triggered by |\n60\t    /// |------|-----|-------------|\n61\t    /// | (new) | Joining | `POST /_miroir/nodes` |\n62\t    /// | Joining | Active | Migration complete |\n63\t    /// | Active | Draining | `POST /_miroir/nodes/{id}/drain` |\n64\t    /// | Draining | Removed | Migration complete |\n65\t    /// | Active/Draining | Failed | Health check detects |\n66\t    /// | Failed | Active | Health check recovery |\n67\t    /// | Active/Failed | Degraded | Partial health |\n68\t    /// | Degraded | Active | Health restored |\n69\t    pub fn can_transition_to(self, new_status: NodeStatus) -> bool {\n70\t        match (self, new_status) {\n71\t            // Initial state\n72\t            (NodeStatus::Joining, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n73\t\n74\t            // Normal operations\n75\t            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Draining) => true,\n76\t            (NodeStatus::Draining, NodeStatus::Removed) => true,\n77\t\n78\t            // Failure and recovery\n79\t            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Failed) => true,\n80\t            (NodeStatus::Draining, NodeStatus::Failed) => true,\n81\t            (NodeStatus::Failed, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n82\t\n83\t            // Degradation\n84\t            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Degraded) => true,\n85\t            (NodeStatus::Failed, NodeStatus::Degraded) => true,\n86\t            (NodeStatus::Degraded, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n87\t\n88\t            // Healthy <-> Active are bidirectional (synonyms)\n89\t            (NodeStatus::Healthy, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n90\t            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Healthy) => true,\n91\t\n92\t            // Same state is always valid\n93\t            (s, t) if s == t => true,\n94\t\n95\t            // All other transitions are invalid\n96\t            _ => false,\n97\t        }\n98\t    }\n99\t\n100\t    /// Returns `true` if the node can accept writes for the given shard.\n101\t    ///\n102\t    /// # Write Eligibility Rules\n103\t    ///\n104\t    /// A node is write-eligible for a shard based on its status:\n105\t    ///\n106\t    /// | Status | Write Eligible | Notes |\n107\t    /// |--------|----------------|-------|\n108\t    /// | Healthy/Active | Yes | Normal operation |\n109\t    /// | Degraded | Yes | Partial failures, still accepting writes |\n110\t    /// | Joining | No | No longer in cluster |\n114\t    ///\n115\t    /// The `draining_shard` parameter should be `Some(shard_id)` if the node\n116\t    /// is in `Draining` status and the shard IS being actively migrated off this node\n117\t    /// (use `None` if the shard is not being drained or no shard is being checked).\n118\t    /// When `Some(...)`, the node is NOT eligible for writes.\n119\t    pub fn is_write_eligible_for(self, draining_shard: Option<u32>) -> bool {\n120\t        match self {\n121\t            NodeStatus::Healthy | NodeStatus::Active | NodeStatus::Degraded => true,\n122\t            NodeStatus::Joining | NodeStatus::Failed | NodeStatus::Removed => false,\n123\t            NodeStatus::Draining => !draining_shard.is_some(),\n124\t        }\n125\t    }\n126\t}\n127\t\n128\timpl fmt::Display for NodeStatus {\n129\t    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n130\t        match self {\n131\t            NodeStatus::Healthy => write!(f, \"healthy\"),\n132\t            NodeStatus::Degraded => write!(f, \"degraded\"),\n133\t            NodeStatus::Active => write!(f, \"active\"),\n134\t            NodeStatus::Joining => write!(f, \"joining\"),\n135\t            NodeStatus::Draining => write!(f, \"draining\"),\n136\t            NodeStatus::Failed => write!(f, \"failed\"),\n137\t            NodeStatus::Removed => write!(f, \"removed\"),\n138\t        }\n139\t    }\n140\t}\n141\t\n142\t/// A single Meilisearch node in the topology.\n143\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n144\tpub struct Node {\n145\t    /// Unique node      self.groups.push(Group::new(self.groups.len() as u32));\n313\t        }\n314\t\n315\t        self.groups[group_id].add_node(node.id.clone());\n316\t        self.nodes.insert(node.id.clone(), Topology management: node registry, groups, and health state.\n\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\nuse std::fmt;\n\n/// Unique identifier for a node.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Hash, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct NodeId(String);\n\nimpl NodeId {\n    /// Create a new NodeId.\n    pub fn new(id: String) -> Self {\n        Self(id)\n    }\n\n    /// Get the node ID as a string slice.\n    pub fn as_str(&self) -> &str {\n        &self.0\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<String> for NodeId {\n    fn from(s: String) -> Self {\n        Self(s)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl AsRef<str> for NodeId {\n    fn as_ref(&self) -> &str {\n        &self.0\n    }\n}\n\n/// Health status of a node.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum NodeStatus {\n    /// Node is healthy and serving traffic.\n    Healthy,\n    /// Node is degraded (intermittent failures, still serving traffic).\n    Degraded,\n    /// Node is active and fully operational (synonym for Healthy).\n    Active,\n    /// Node is joining the cluster (being provisioned).\n    Joining,\n    /// Node is draining (graceful shutdown, not accepting new writes).\n    Draining,\n    /// Node has failed (unplanned outage).\n    Failed,\n    /// Node has been removed from the cluster (tracked for migration).\n    Removed,\n}\n\nimpl NodeStatus {\n    /// Check if a transition from `self` to `new_status` is valid.\n    ///\n    /// # State Transition Rules\n    ///\n    /// | From | To | Triggered by |\n    /// |------|-----|-------------|\n    /// | (new) | Joining | `POST /_miroir/nodes` |\n    /// | Joining | Active | Migration complete |\n    /// | Active | Draining | `POST /_miroir/nodes/{id}/drain` |\n    /// | Draining | Removed | Migration complete |\n    /// | Active/Draining | Failed | Health check detects |\n    /// | Failed | Active | Health check recovery |\n    /// | Active/Failed | Degraded | Partial health |\n    /// | Degraded | Active | Health restored |\n    pub fn can_transition_to(self, new_status: NodeStatus) -> bool {\n        match (self, new_status) {\n            // Initial state\n            (NodeStatus::Joining, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n\n            // Normal operations\n            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Draining) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Draining, NodeStatus::Removed) => true,\n\n            // Failure and recovery\n            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Failed) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Draining, NodeStatus::Failed) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Failed, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n\n            // Degradation\n            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Degraded) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Failed, NodeStatus::Degraded) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Degraded, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n\n            // Healthy <-> Active are bidirectional (synonyms)\n            (NodeStatus::Healthy, NodeStatus::Active) => true,\n            (NodeStatus::Active, NodeStatus::Healthy) => true,\n\n            // Same state is always valid\n            (s, t) if s == t => true,\n\n            // All other transitions are invalid\n            _ => false,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns `true` if the node can accept writes for the given shard.\n    ///\n    /// # Write Eligibility Rules\n    ///\n    /// A node is write-eligible for a shard based on its status:\n    ///\n    /// | Status | Write Eligible | Notes |\n    /// |--------|----------------|-------|\n    /// | Healthy/Active | Yes | Normal operation |\n    /// | Degraded | Yes | Partial failures, still accepting writes |\n    /// | Joining | No | Being provisioned, not yet ready |\n    /// | Draining | Conditional | Only for shards it still owns during migration |\n    /// | Failed | No | Unavailable |\n    /// | Removed | No | No longer in cluster |\n    ///\n    /// The `draining_shard` parameter should be `Some(shard_id)` if the node\n    /// is in `Draining` status and the shard IS being actively migrated off this node\n    /// (use `None` if the shard is not being drained or no shard is being checked).\n    /// When `Some(...)`, the node is NOT eligible for writes.\n    pub fn is_write_eligible_for(self, draining_shard: Option<u32>) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            NodeStatus::Healthy | NodeStatus::Active | NodeStatus::Degraded => true,\n            NodeStatus::Joining | NodeStatus::Failed | NodeStatus::Removed => false,\n            NodeStatus::Draining => !draining_shard.is_some(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for NodeStatus {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            NodeStatus::Healthy => write!(f, \"healthy\"),\n            NodeStatus::Degraded => write!(f, \"degraded\"),\n            NodeStatus::Active => write!(f, \"active\"),\n            NodeStatus::Joining => write!(f, \"joining\"),\n            NodeStatus::Draining => write!(f, \"draining\"),\n            NodeStatus::Failed => write!(f, \"failed\"),\n            NodeStatus::Removed => write!(f, \"removed\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// A single Meilisearch node in the topology.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Node {\n    /// Unique node identifier.\n    pub id: NodeId,\n\n    /// Node base URL / address.\n    pub address: String,\n\n    /// Current health status.\n    pub status: NodeStatus,\n\n    /// Replica group assignment (0-based).\n    pub replica_group: u32,\n}\n\nimpl Node {\n    /// Create a new node.\n    pub fn new(id: NodeId, address: String, replica_group: u32) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id,\n            address,\n            status: NodeStatus::Joining,\n            replica_group,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Create a new node with a specific status.\n    pub fn with_status(id: NodeId, address: String, replica_group: u32, status: NodeStatus) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id,\n            address,\n            status,\n            replica_group,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Check if the node is healthy (can serve traffic).\n    pub fn is_healthy(&self) -> bool {\n        matches!(self.status, NodeStatus::Healthy | NodeStatus::Active)\n    }\n\n    /// Transition the node to a new status, validating the transition.\n    ///\n    /// Returns `Ok(())` if the transition is valid, `Err` otherwise.\n    pub fn set_status(&mut self, new_status: NodeStatus) -> Result<(), TransitionError> {\n        if self.status.can_transition_to(new_status) {\n            self.status = new_status;\n            Ok(())\n        } else {\n            Err(TransitionError {\n                from: self.status,\n                to: new_status,\n            })\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Check if the node is eligible to receive writes for a specific shard.\n    ///\n    /// For nodes in `Draining` status, this depends on whether the shard is\n    /// being actively migrated off this node. The caller should pass\n    /// `Some(shard_id)` if the shard is being drained from this node.\n    pub fn is_write_eligible_for(&self, shard_id: Option<u32>) -> bool {\n        self.status.is_write_eligible_for(shard_id)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Error returned when an invalid state transition is attempted.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct TransitionError {\n    pub from: NodeStatus,\n    pub to: NodeStatus,\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for TransitionError {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(\n            f,\n            \"invalid state transition from {} to {}\",\n            self.from, self.to\n        )\n    }\n}\n\nimpl std::error::Error for TransitionError {}\n\n/// A replica group: an independent query pool.\n///\n/// Each group holds all S shards, distributed across its nodes.\n/// Reads are routed to a single group per query.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Group {\n    /// Group identifier (0-based).\n    pub id: u32,\n\n    /// Nodes in this group.\n    nodes: Vec<NodeId>,\n}\n\nimpl Group {\n    /// Create a new group.\n    pub fn new(id: u32) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id,\n            nodes: Vec::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Add a node to this group.\n    pub fn add_node(&mut self, node_id: NodeId) {\n        if !self.nodes.contains(&node_id) {\n            self.nodes.push(node_id);\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get the node IDs in this group.\n    pub fn nodes(&self) -> &[NodeId] {\n        &self.nodes\n    }\n\n    /// Get the number of nodes in this group.\n    pub fn node_count(&self) -> usize {\n        self.nodes.len()\n    }\n\n    /// Get all healthy nodes in this group, looking them up from the topology.\n    ///\n    /// This requires access to the topology's node map to resolve NodeIds to Nodes.\n    pub fn healthy_nodes<'a>(&'a self, all_nodes: &'a HashMap<NodeId, Node>) -> Vec<&'a Node> {\n        self.nodes\n            .iter()\n            .filter_map(|node_id| all_nodes.get(node_id))\n            .filter(|node| node.is_healthy())\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Cluster topology: groups, nodes, and health state.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Topology {\n    /// All nodes in the cluster.\n    nodes: HashMap<NodeId, Node>,\n\n    /// Replica groups.\n    groups: Vec<Group>,\n\n    /// Replication factor (intra-group).\n    rf: usize,\n\n    /// Total number of logical shards (S).\n    shards: u32,\n}\n\nimpl Topology {\n    /// Create a new empty topology.\n    pub fn new(shards: u32, rf: usize) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            nodes: HashMap::new(),\n            groups: Vec::new(),\n            rf,\n            shards,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Add a node to the topology.\n    pub fn add_node(&mut self, node: Node) {\n        let group_id = node.replica_group as usize;\n\n        // Ensure group exists\n        while self.groups.len() <= group_id {\n            self.groups.push(Group::new(self.groups.len() as u32));\n        }\n\n        self.groups[group_id].add_node(node.id.clone());\n        self.nodes.insert(node.id.clone(), node);\n    }\n\n    /// Get a node by ID.\n    pub fn node(&self, id: &NodeId) -> Option<&Node> {\n        self.nodes.get(id)\n    }\n\n    /// Get a mutable reference to a node by ID.\n    pub fn node_mut(&mut self, id: &NodeId) -> Option<&mut Node> {\n        self.nodes.get_mut(id)\n    }\n\n    /// Get all nodes.\n    pub fn nodes(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &Node> {\n        self.nodes.values()\n    }\n\n    /// Get a group by ID.\n    pub fn group(&self, id: u32) -> Option<&Group> {\n        self.groups.get(id as usize)\n    }\n\n    /// Iterate over all groups.\n    pub fn groups(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &Group> {\n        self.groups.iter()\n    }\n\n    /// Get the replication factor.\n    pub fn rf(&self) -> usize {\n        self.rf\n    }\n\n    /// Get the number of shards.\n    pub fn shards(&self) -> u32 {\n        self.shards\n    }\n\n    /// Get the number of replica groups.\n    pub fn replica_group_count(&self) -> u32 {\n        self.groups.len() as u32\n    }\n\n    /// Get healthy nodes in a specific group.\n    pub fn healthy_nodes_in_group(&self, group_id: u32) -> Vec<&Node> {\n        self.group(group_id)\n            .map(|g| g.healthy_nodes(&self.nodes))\n            .unwrap_or_default()\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    // --- Existing tests updated for address field ---\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_node_is_healthy() {\n        let mut node = Node::new(\n            NodeId::new(\"node1\".to_string()),\n            \"http://example.com\".to_string(),\n            0,\n        );\n\n        // Joining status is not healthy\n        assert!(!node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Healthy status is healthy\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Healthy;\n        assert!(node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Active status is healthy (synonym for Healthy)\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Active;\n        assert!(node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Degraded status is not healthy (intermittent failures)\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Degraded;\n        assert!(!node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Draining status is not healthy\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Draining;\n        assert!(!node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Failed status is not healthy\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Failed;\n        assert!(!node.is_healthy());\n\n        // Removed status is not healthy\n        node.status = NodeStatus::Removed;\n        assert!(!node.is_healthy());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_group_node_count() {\n        let mut group = Group::new(0);\n        assert_eq!(group.node_count(), 0);\n\n        group.add_node(NodeId::new(\"node1\".to_string()));\n        assert_eq!(group.node_count(), 1);\n\n        group.add_node(NodeId::new(\"node2\".to_string()));\n        assert_eq!(group.node_count(), 2);\n\n        // Adding duplicate node doesn't increase count\n        group.add_node(NodeId::new(\"node1\".to_string()));\n        assert_eq!(group.node_count(), 2);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_topology_replica_group_count() {\n        let mut topology = Topology::new(64, 2);\n\n        // Empty topology has 0 groups\n        assert_eq!(topology.replica_group_count(), 0);\n\n        // Add nodes to group 0\n        topology.add_node(Node::new(\n            NodeId::new(\"node1\".to_string()),\n            \"http://example.com\".to_string(),\n            0,\n        ));\n        assert_eq!(topology.replica_group_count(), 1);\n\n        // Add nodes to group 1\n        topology.add_node(Node::new(\n            NodeId::new(\"node2\".to_string()),\n            \"http://example.com\".to_string(),\n            1,\n        ));\n        assert_eq!(topology.replica_group_count(), 2);\n\n        // Add more nodes to existing groups\n Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n2\t\n3\tuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\n4\tuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\n5\tuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n6\t\n7\t/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n8\t///\n9\t/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\n10\t///\n11\t/// CRITICAL: Uses seed 0 to match Meilisearch Enterprise's hash function.\n12\t/// Any deviation (different seed, different ordering, endianness) forks\n13\t/// routing across any two Miroir instances and silently corrupts writes.\n14\tpub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n15\t    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n16\t    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n17\t    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n18\t    h.finish()\n19\t}\n20\t\n21\t/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n22\t///\n23\t/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\n24\t///\n25\t/// Nodes are sorted by score descending, with ties broken lexicographically\n26\t/// by node_id to ensure deterministic assignment even when hash scores collide.\n27\tpub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n28\t    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n29\t        .iter()\n30\t        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n31\t        .collect();\n32\t    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| {\n33\t        b.0.cmp(&a.0)\n34\t            .then_with(|| a.1.as_str().cmp(b.1.as_str()))\n35\t    });\n36\t    scored\n37\t        .into_iter()\n38\t        .take(rf)\n39\t        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n40\t        .collect()\n41\t}\n42\t\n43\t/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\n44\tpub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n45\t    topology\n46\t        .groups()\n47\t        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n48\t        .collect()\n49\t}\n50\t\n51\t/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\n52\tpub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n53\t    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n54\t}\n55\t\n56\t/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\n57\t///\n58\t/// Returns a Vec where index i contains the node to query for shard i.\n59\t/// The length is always exactly shard_count, even if multiple shards\n60\t/// map to the same node.\n61\tpub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: replicas for intra-group load balancing\n66\t            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n67\t        })\n68\t        .collect()\n69\t}\n70\t\n71\t/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\n72\tpub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n73\t    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n74\t    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n75\t    (h.finish() % Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\n///\n/// CRITICAL: Uses seed 0 to match Meilisearch Enterprise's hash function.\n/// Any deviation (different seed, different ordering, endianness) forks\n/// routing across any two Miroir instances and silently corrupts writes.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\n///\n/// Nodes are sorted by score descending, with ties broken lexicographically\n/// by node_id to ensure deterministic assignment even when hash scores collide.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| {\n        b.0.cmp(&a.0)\n            .then_with(|| a.1.as_str().cmp(b.1.as_str()))\n    });\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\n///\n/// Returns a Vec where index i contains the node to query for shard i.\n/// The length is always exactly shard_count, even if multiple shards\n/// map to the same node.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use crate::topology::{Node, NodeId};\n\n    // Test 1: Rendezvous assignment is deterministic given fixed node list\n    #[test]\n    fn test_rendezvous_determinism() {\n        let nodes: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let shard_id = 42;\n\n        let assignment1 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n        let assignment2 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n\n        assert_eq!(assignment1, assignment2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 2: Score is stable across calls\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_stability() {\n        let score1 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        assert_eq!(score1, score2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 3: Different shard+node pairs produce different scores\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_uniqueness() {\n        let score1 = score(1, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(1, \"node2\");\n        let score3 = score(2, \"node1\");\n\n        assert_ne!(score1, score2);\n        assert_ne!(score1, score3);\n        assert_ne!(score2, score3);\n    }\n\n    // Test 4: Adding a 4th node moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_minimal_reshuffling_on_add() {\n        let nodes_3: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let nodes_4: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n\n        let shard_count = 100;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut moved_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Shard moved if its primary owner changed\n            if assign_3.first() != assign_4.first() {\n                moved_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Expected: at most ~2 × (1/4) = 50% of shards\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.5).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            moved_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {max_expected} shards to move, but {moved_count} moved\"\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 5: 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each node holds 18–26 shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_distribution_64_3_rf1() {\n        let nodes: = 1;\n\n        let mut node_shard_counts: std::collections::HashMap<String, usize> =\n            std::collections::HashMap::new();\n\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let .entry(node.as_str().to_string())\n                    .or_insert(0) += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Debug: print actual distribution\n        eprintln!(\"Actual shard distribution: {node_shard_counts:?}\");\n\n        // DoD requirement: each node holds 15–27 shards\n        // This accommodates natural variance in hash-based distribution\n        for (node, count) in &node_shard_counts {\n            assert!(\n                *count >= 15 && *count <= 27,\n                \"Node {node} has {count} shards, expected 15–27\"\n            );\n        }\n\n        // minimally on add/remove\n    #[test]\n    fn test_top_rf_stability() {\n        let nodes_3: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let nodes_4: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let rf = 2;\n        let shard_count = 100;\n\n        let mut changed_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Count how many of the top-RF nodes changed\n            let set_3: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_3.iter().collect();\n            let set_4: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_4.iter().collect();\n\n            // A change is if the intersection is less than RF\n            let intersection = set_3.intersection(&set_4).count();\n            if intersection < rf {\n                changed_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Adding a 4th node affects approximately 1/4 of assignments\n        // But with RF=2, we need to account for overlap\n        // Expected: roughly 50-60% might have some change\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.6).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            changed_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {max_expected} shards to change, but {changed_count} It:\n59\t/// 1. Collects all hits with scores from all shards\n60\t/// 2. Sorts globally by `_rankingScore` descending\n61\t/// 3. Applies offset + limit after merge\n62\t/// 4. Strips `_rankingScore` if client didn't request it\n63\t/// 5. Always strips `_miroir_*` reserved fields\n64\t/// 6. Sums facet counts across shards\n65\t/// 7. Sums `estimatedTotalHits` across shards\n66\t/// 8. Takes max `processingTimeMs` across shards\n67\t///\n68\t/// Uses a binary min-heap to avoid keeping all hits in RAM when fan-out is large.\n69\t/// Uses BTreeMap for stable facet serialization (deterministic JSON output).\n70\tpub fn merge(input: MergeInput) -> MergedSearchResult {\n71\t    // Filter to only successful responses\n72\t    let successful_shards: Vec<_> = input\n73\t        .shard_hits\n74\t        .iter()\n75\t        .filter(|s| s.success)\n76\t        .collect();\n77\t\n78\t    // Check if any shards failed (degraded mode)\n79\t    let degraded = successful_shards.len() < input.shard_hits.len();\n80\t\n81\t    // Collect all hits with their ranking scores and primary keys\n82\t    let mut all_hits: Vec<HitWithScore> = Vec::new();\n83\t\n84\t    for shard in &successful_shards {\n85\t        if let Some(hits) = shard.body.get(\"hits\").and_then(|h| h.as_array()) {\n86\t            for hit in hits {\n87\t                let score = hit\n88\t                    .get(\"_rankingScore\")\n89\t                    .and_then(|s| s.as_f64())\n90\t                    .unwrap_or(0.0);\n91\t\n92\t                let primary_key = hit\n93\t                    .get(\"id\")\n94\t                    .and_then(|id| id.as_str())\n95\t                    .unwrap_or(\"\")\n96\t                    .to_string();\n97\t\n98\t                all_hits.push(HitWithScore {\n99\t                    score,\n100\t                    primary_key,\n101\t                    hit: hit.clone(),\n102\t                });\n103\t            }\n104\t        }\n105\t    }\n106\t\n107\t    // Use a min-heap of size offset + limit to avoid keeping all hits in RAM\n108\t    let heap_size = input.offset + input.limit;\n109\t    let top_hits = if all_hits.len() > heap_size * 2 {\n110\t        // Only use heap optimization if we have significantly more hits than needed\n111\t        // Use BinaryHeap with Reverse to get min-heap behavior\n112\t        // Reverse<T> makes the \"smallest\" T become the \"largest\" Reverse<T>\n113\t        // So in BinaryHeap (max-heap), the smallest T ends up at the top\n114\t        use std::cmp::Reverse;\n115\t\n116\t        // First, define a wrapper with natural ascending order by score\n117\t        #[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\n118\t        struct AscendingHit(HitWithScore);\n119\t\n120\t        impl PartialOrd for AscendingHit {\n121\t            fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<std::cmp::Ordering> {\n122\t                Some(self.cmp(other))\n123\t            }\n124\t        }\n125\t\n126\t        impl Ord for AscendingHit {\n127\t            fn cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n128\t                // Ascending order: lower score first, then primary key ascending\n129\t                match self.0.score.partial_cmp(&other.0.score) {\n130\t                    Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n131\t                        self.0.primary_key.cmp(&other.0.primary_key)\n132\t                    }\n133\t                    Some(ord) => ord,\n134\t                }\n135\t            }\n136\t        }\n137\t\n138\t        // Reverse<AscendingHit> in BinaryHeap gives us a min-heap by score\n139\t        // The lowest score (worst) will be at the top for easy replacement\n140\t        let mut heap: BinaryHeap<Reverse<AscendingHit>> = BinaryHeap::new();\n141\t\n142\t        for hit in all_hits {\n143\t            if heap.len() < heap_size {\n144\t                heap.push(Reverse(AscendingHit(hit)));\n145\t            } else {\n146\t                // Peek at the smallest (worst) hit in our top-k\n147\t                if let Some(Reverse(worst)) = heap.peek() {\n148\t                    // If current hit is better than our worst, replace it\n149\t                    // Compare using the score directly\n150\t                    if hit.score > worst.0.score ||\n151\t                       (hit.score == worst.0.score && hit.primary_key < worst.0.primary_key) {\n152\t                        heap.pop();\n153\t                        heap.push(Reverse(AscendingHit(hit)));\n154\t                    }\n155\t                }\n156\t            }\n157\t        }\n158\t\n159\t        // Convert to sorted vector (descending by score)\n160\t        let mut result: Vec<_> = heap.into_iter().map(|r| (r.0).0).collect();\n161\t        result.sort_by(|a, b| a.descending_cmp(b));\n162\t        result\n163\t    } else {\n164\t        // For smaller result sets, just sort directly\n165\t        all_hits.sort_by(|a, b| a.descending_cmp(b));\n166\t        all_hits\n167\t    };\n168\t\n169\t    // Apply offset and limit\n170\t    let page: Vec<Value> = top_hits\n171\t        .into_iter()\n172\t        .skip(input.offset)\n173\t        .take(input.limit)\n174\t        .map(|mut hit_with_score| {\n175\t            let hit = &mut hit_with_score.hit;\n176\t\n177\t            // Strip all _miroir_* fields (always removed)\n178\t            if let Some(obj) = hit.as_object_mut() {\n179\t                obj.retain(|k, _| !k.starts_with(\"_miroir_\"));\n180\t            }\n181\t\n182\t            // Strip _rankingScore if client didn't request it\n183\t            if !input.client_requested_score {\n184\t                if let Some(obj) = hit.as_object_mut() {\n185\t                    obj.remove(\"_rankingScore\");\n186\t                }\n187\t            }\n188\t\n189\t            hit.clone()\n190\t        })\n191\t        .collect();\n192\t\n193\t    // Aggregate facets across all shards\n194\t    let facets = merge_facets(&successful_shards, input.facets.as_deref());\n195\t\n196\t    // Sum estimated total hits\n197\t    let estimated_total_hits: u64 = successful_shards\n198\t        .iter()\n199\t        .filter_map(|s| s.body.get(\"estimatedTotalHits\").and_then(|v| v.as_u64()))\n200\t        .sum();\n201\t\n202\t    // Max processing time across all shards\n203\t    let processing_time_ms: u64 = successful_shards\n204\t        .iter()\n205\t        .filter_map(|s| s.body.get(\"processingTimeMs\").and_then(|v| v.as_u64()))\n206\t        .max()\n207\t        .unwrap_or(0);\n208\t\n209\t    MergedSearchResult {\n210\t        hits: page,\n211\t        facets,\n212\t        estimated_total_hits,\n213\t        processing_time_ms,\n214\t        degraded,\n215\t    }\n216\t}\n217\t\n218\t/// A hit with its ranking score for sorting.\n219\t#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\n220\tstruct HitWithScore {\n221\t    score: f64,\n222\t    primary_key: String,\n223\t    hit: Value,\n224\t}\n225\t\n226\timpl PartialEq for HitWithScore {\n227\t    fn eq(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {\n228\t        self.score == other.score && self.primary_key == other.primary_key\n229\t    }\n230\t}\n231\t\n232\timpl Eq for HitWithScore {}\n233\t\n234\timpl PartialOrd for HitWithScore {\n235\t    fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<std::cmp::Ordering> {\n236\t        Some(self.cmp(other))\n237\t    }\n238\t}\n239\t\n240\timpl HitWithScore {\n241\t    /// Compare for descending order (score desc, primary key asc).\n242\t    fn descending_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n243\t        // Sort by score descending, then by primary key ascending for tie-breaking\n244\t        match other.score.partial_cmp(&self.score) {\n245\t            Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n246\t                // On equal scores (or NaN), fall back to primary key ascending\n247\t                self.primary_key.cmp(&other.primary_key)\n248\t            }\n249\t            Some(ord) => ord,\n250\t        }\n251\t    }\n252\t}\n253\t\n254\timpl Ord for HitWithScore {\n255\t    fn cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n256\t        // Sort by score descending, then by primary key ascending for tie-breaking\n257\t        match self.score.partial_cmp(&other.score) {\n258\t            Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n259\t                // On equal scores (or NaN), fall back to primary key\n260\t                // Reversed for descending order\n261\t                other.primary_key.cmp(&self.primary_key)\n262\t            }\n263\t            Some(ord) => ord.reverse(),\n264\t        }\n265\t    }\n266\t}\n267\t\n268\t/// Result merger: combines responses from multiple shards.\n269\tpub trait Merger: Send + Sync {\n270\t    /// Merge search results from multiple shards.\n271\t    ///\n272\t    /// Takes the raw JSON responses from each shard and produces\n273\t    /// a merged result with global sorting, offset/limit applied,\n274\t    /// and facet aggregation.\n275\t    fn merge(\n276\t        &self,\n277\t        shard_responses: Vec<ShardResponse>,\n278\t        offset: usize,\n279\t        limit: usize,\n280\t        client_requested_score: bool,\n281\t    ) -> Result<MergedResult>;\n282\t}\n283\t\n284\t/// Response from a single shard.\n285\t#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\n286\tpub struct ShardResponse {\n287\t    /// Shard identifier.\n288\t    pub shard_id: u32,\n289\t\n290\t    /// Raw JSON response from the node.\n291\t    pub body: Value,\n292\t\n293\t    /// Whether this shard succeeded.\n294\t    pub success: bool,\n295\t}\n296\t\n297\t/// Merged search result (legacy, use MergedSearchResult instead).\n298\t#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\n299\tpub struct MergedResult {\n300\t    /// Merged hits (globally sorted, offset/limit applied).\n301\t    pub hits: Vec<Value>,\n302\t\n303\t    /// Aggregated facets.\n304\t    pub facets: Value,\n305\t\n306\t    /// Estimated total hits (sum of shard totals).\n307\t    pub total_hits: u64,\n308\t\n309\t    /// Processing time in milliseconds.\n310\t    pub processing_time_ms: u64,\n311\t\n312\t    /// Whether the response is degraded (some shards failed).\n313\t    pub degraded: bool,\n314\t}\n315\t\n316\t/// Default implementation of Merger.\n317\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]\n318\tpub struct MergerImpl;\n319\t\n320\timpl Merger for MergerImpl {\n321\t    fn merge(\n322\t        &self,\n323\t        shard_responses: Vec<ShardResponse>,\n324\t        offset: usize,\n325\t        limit: usize,\n326\t        client_requested_score: bool,\n327\t    ) -> Result<MergedResult> {\n328\t        // Convert ShardResponse to ShardHitPage\n329\t        let shard_hits: Vec<ShardHitPage> = shard_responses\n330\t            .into_iter()\n331\t            .map(|sr| ShardHitPage {\n332\t                body: sr.body,\n333\t                success: sr.success,\n334\t            })\n335\t            .collect();\n336\t\n337\t        // Call the new merge function\n338\t        let input = MergeInput {\n339\t            shard_hits,\n340\t            offset,\n341\t            limit,\n342\t            client_requested_score,\n343\t            facets: None,\n344\t        };\n345\t\n346\t        let result = merge(input);\n347\t\n348\t        Ok(MergedResult {\n349\t            hits: result.hits,\n350\t            facets: result.facets,\n351\t            total_hits: result.estimated_total_hits,\n352\t            processing_time_ms: result.processing_time_ms,\n353\t            degraded: result.degraded,\n354\t        })\n355\t    }\n356\t}\n357\t\n358\t/// Merge facet distributions from all shards.\n359\t///\n360\t/// Facets are nested objects like `{\"color\": {\"red\": 10, \"blue\": 5}}`.\n361\t/// We sum counts for each facet value across all shards.\n362\t///\n363\t/// Uses BTreeMap for stable, deterministic serialization.\n364\tfn merge_facets(shards: &[&ShardHitPage], facet_filter: Option<&[String]>) -> Value {\n365\t    let mut merged_facets: BTreeMap<String, BTreeMap<String, u64>> = BTreeMap::new();\n366\t\n367\t    for shard in shards {\n368\t        if let Some(facets) = shard\n369\t            .body\n370\t            .get(\"facetDistribution\")\n371\t            .and_then(|f| f.as_object())\n372\t        {\n373\t            for (facet_name, facet_values) in facets {\n374\t                // Apply facet filter if provided\n375\t                if let Some(filter) = facet_filter {\n376\t                    if !filter.contains(&facet_name) {\n377\t                        continue;\n378\t                    }\n379\t                }\n380\t\n381\t                if let Some(values_obj) = facet_values.as_object() {\n382\t                    let entry = merged_facets.entry(facet_name.clone()).or_default();\n383\t\n384\t                    for (value, count) in values_obj {\n385\t                        let count_val = count.as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n386\t                        *entry.entry(value.clone()).or_insert(0) += count_val;\n387\t                    }\n388\t                }\n389\t            }\n390\t        }\n391\t    }\n392\t\n393\t    // Convert back to JSON structure (BTreeMap ensures stable key order)\n394\t    let result: serde_json::Map<String, Value> = merged_facets\n395\t        .into_iter()\n396\t        .map(|(facet_name, values)| {\n397\t            let values_obj: serde_json::Map<String, Value> = values\n398\t                .into_iter()\n399\t                .map(|(k, v)| (k, Value::Number(v.into())))\n400\t                .collect();\n401\t            (facet_name, Value::Object(values_obj))\n402\t        })\n403\t        .collect();\n404\t\n405\t    Value::Object(result)\n406\t}\n407\t\n408\t/// Stub implementation that returns empty results.\n409\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]\n410\tpub struct StubMerger;\n411\t\n412\timpl Merger for StubMerger {\n413\t    fn merge(\n414\t        &self,\n415\t        _shard_responses: Vec<ShardResponse>,\n416\t        _offset: usize,\n417\t        _limit: usize,\n418\t        _client_requested_score: bool,\n419\t    ) -> Result<MergedResult> {\n420\t        Ok(MergedResult {\n421\t            hits: Vec::new(),\n422\t            facets: serde_json::json!({}),\n423\t            total_hits: 0,\n424\t            processing_time_ms: 0,\n425\t            degraded: false,\n426\t        })\n427\t    }\n428\t}\n429\t\n430\t#[cfg(test)]\n431\tmod tests {\n432\t    use super::*;\n433\t\n434\t    fn create_hit(score: f64, id: &str) -> Value {\n435\t        serde_json::json!({\n436\t Result merger: combines shard results into a single response.\n\nuse crate::Result;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse serde_json::Value;\nuse std::collections::{BTreeMap, BinaryHeap};\n\n/// Input to the merge function.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MergeInput {\n    /// One page of hits per node in the covering set.\n    pub shard_hits: Vec<ShardHitPage>,\n\n    /// Offset to apply after merge.\n    pub offset: usize,\n\n    /// Limit to apply after merge.\n    pub limit: usize,\n\n    /// Whether the client requested the ranking score in the response.\n    pub client_requested_score: bool,\n\n    /// Facet names to include (if None, include all).\n    pub facets: Option<Vec<String>>,\n}\n\n/// A page of hits from a single shard.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ShardHitPage {\n    /// Raw JSON response from the node.\n    pub body: Value,\n\n    /// Whether this shard succeeded.\n    pub success: bool,\n}\n\n/// Merged search result.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MergedSearchResult {\n    /// Merged hits (globally sorted, offset/limit applied).\n    pub hits: Vec<Value>,\n\n    /// Aggregated facets.\n    pub facets: Value,\n\n    /// Estimated total hits (sum of shard totals).\n    pub estimated_total_hits: u64,\n\n    /// Processing time in milliseconds.\n    pub processing_time_ms: u64,\n\n    /// Whether the response is degraded (some shards failed).\n    pub degraded: bool,\n}\n\n/// Merge search results from multiple shards.\n///\n/// This is the primary entry point for result merging. It:\n/// 1. Collects all hits with scores from all shards\n/// 2. Sorts globally by `_rankingScore` descending\n/// 3. Applies offset + limit after merge\n/// 4. Strips `_rankingScore` if client didn't request it\n/// 5. Always strips `_miroir_*` reserved fields\n/// 6. Sums facet counts across shards\n/// 7. Sums `estimatedTotalHits` across shards\n/// 8. Takes max `processingTimeMs` across shards\n///\n/// Uses a binary min-heap to avoid keeping all hits in RAM when fan-out is large.\n/// Uses BTreeMap for stable facet serialization (deterministic JSON output).\npub fn merge(input: MergeInput) -> MergedSearchResult {\n    // Filter to only successful responses\n    let successful_shards: Vec<_> = input\n        .shard_hits\n        .iter()\n        .filter(|s| s.success)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Check if any shards failed (degraded mode)\n    let degraded = successful_shards.len() < input.shard_hits.len();\n\n    // Collect all hits with their ranking scores and primary keys\n    let mut all_hits: Vec<HitWithScore> = Vec::new();\n\n    for shard in &successful_shards {\n        if let Some(hits) = shard.body.get(\"hits\").and_then(|h| h.as_array()) {\n            for hit in hits {\n                let score = hit\n                    .get(\"_rankingScore\")\n                    .and_then(|s| s.as_f64())\n                    .unwrap_or(0.0);\n\n                let primary_key = hit\n                    .get(\"id\")\n                    .and_then(|id| id.as_str())\n                    .unwrap_or(\"\")\n                    .to_string();\n\n                all_hits.push(HitWithScore {\n                    score,\n                    primary_key,\n                    hit: hit.clone(),\n                });\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Use a min-heap of size offset + limit to avoid keeping all hits in RAM\n    let heap_size = input.offset + input.limit;\n    let top_hits = if all_hits.len() > heap_size * 2 {\n        // Only use heap optimization if we have significantly more hits than needed\n        // Use BinaryHeap with Reverse to get min-heap behavior\n        // Reverse<T> makes the \"smallest\" T become the \"largest\" Reverse<T>\n        // So in BinaryHeap (max-heap), the smallest T ends up at the top\n        use std::cmp::Reverse;\n\n        // First, define a wrapper with natural ascending order by score\n        #[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\n        struct AscendingHit(HitWithScore);\n\n        impl PartialOrd for AscendingHit {\n            fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<std::cmp::Ordering> {\n                Some(self.cmp(other))\n            }\n        }\n\n        impl Ord for AscendingHit {\n            fn cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n                // Ascending order: lower score first, then primary key ascending\n                match self.0.score.partial_cmp(&other.0.score) {\n                    Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n                        self.0.primary_key.cmp(&other.0.primary_key)\n                    }\n                    Some(ord) => ord,\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Reverse<AscendingHit> in BinaryHeap gives us a min-heap by score\n        // The lowest score (worst) will be at the top for easy replacement\n        let mut heap: BinaryHeap<Reverse<AscendingHit>> = BinaryHeap::new();\n\n        for hit in all_hits {\n            if heap.len() < heap_size {\n                heap.push(Reverse(AscendingHit(hit)));\n            } else {\n                // Peek at the smallest (worst) hit in our top-k\n                if let Some(Reverse(worst)) = heap.peek() {\n                    // If current hit is better than our worst, replace it\n                    // Compare using the score directly\n                    if hit.score > worst.0.score ||\n                       (hit.score == worst.0.score && hit.primary_key < worst.0.primary_key) {\n                        heap.pop();\n                        heap.push(Reverse(AscendingHit(hit)));\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Convert to sorted vector (descending by score)\n        let mut result: Vec<_> = heap.into_iter().map(|r| (r.0).0).collect();\n        result.sort_by(|a, b| a.descending_cmp(b));\n        result\n    } else {\n        // For smaller result sets, just sort directly\n        all_hits.sort_by(|a, b| a.descending_cmp(b));\n        all_hits\n    };\n\n    // Apply offset and limit\n    let page: Vec<Value> = top_hits\n        .into_iter()\n        .skip(input.offset)\n        .take(input.limit)\n        .map(|mut hit_with_score| {\n            let hit = &mut hit_with_score.hit;\n\n            // Strip all _miroir_* fields (always removed)\n            if let Some(obj) = hit.as_object_mut() {\n                obj.retain(|k, _| !k.starts_with(\"_miroir_\"));\n            }\n\n            // Strip _rankingScore if client didn't request it\n            if !input.client_requested_score {\n                if let Some(obj) = hit.as_object_mut() {\n                    obj.remove(\"_rankingScore\");\n                }\n            }\n\n            hit.clone()\n        })\n        .collect();\n\n    // Aggregate facets across all shards\n    let facets = merge_facets(&successful_shards, input.facets.as_deref());\n\n    // Sum estimated total hits\n    let estimated_total_hits: u64 = successful_shards\n        .iter()\n        .filter_map(|s| s.body.get(\"estimatedTotalHits\").and_then(|v| v.as_u64()))\n        .sum();\n\n    // Max processing time across all shards\n    let processing_time_ms: u64 = successful_shards\n        .iter()\n        .filter_map(|s| s.body.get(\"processingTimeMs\").and_then(|v| v.as_u64()))\n        .max()\n        .unwrap_or(0);\n\n    MergedSearchResult {\n        hits: page,\n        facets,\n        estimated_total_hits,\n        processing_time_ms,\n        degraded,\n    }\n}\n\n/// A hit with its ranking score for sorting.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\nstruct HitWithScore {\n    score: f64,\n    primary_key: String,\n    hit: Value,\n}\n\nimpl PartialEq for HitWithScore {\n    fn eq(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {\n        self.score == other.score && self.primary_key == other.primary_key\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Eq for HitWithScore {}\n\nimpl PartialOrd for HitWithScore {\n    fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<std::cmp::Ordering> {\n        Some(self.cmp(other))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HitWithScore {\n    /// Compare for descending order (score desc, primary key asc).\n    fn descending_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n        // Sort by score descending, then by primary key ascending for tie-breaking\n        match other.score.partial_cmp(&self.score) {\n            Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n                // On equal scores (or NaN), fall back to primary key ascending\n                self.primary_key.cmp(&other.primary_key)\n            }\n            Some(ord) => ord,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Ord for HitWithScore {\n    fn cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> std::cmp::Ordering {\n        // Sort by score descending, then by primary key ascending for tie-breaking\n        match self.score.partial_cmp(&other.score) {\n            Some(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal) | None => {\n                // On equal scores (or NaN), fall back to primary key\n                // Reversed for descending order\n                other.primary_key.cmp(&self.primary_key)\n            }\n            Some(ord) => ord.reverse(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Result merger: combines responses from multiple shards.\npub trait Merger: Send + Sync {\n    /// Merge search results from multiple shards.\n    ///\n    /// Takes the raw JSON responses from each shard and produces\n    /// a merged result with global sorting, offset/limit applied,\n    /// and facet aggregation.\n    fn merge(\n        &self,\n        shard_responses: Vec<ShardResponse>,\n        offset: usize,\n        limit: usize,\n        client_requested_score: bool,\n    ) -> Result<MergedResult>;\n}\n\n/// Response from a single shard.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct ShardResponse {\n    /// Shard identifier.\n    pub shard_id: u32,\n\n    /// Raw JSON response from the node.\n    pub body: Value,\n\n    /// Whether this shard succeeded.\n    pub success: bool,\n}\n\n/// Merged search result (legacy, use MergedSearchResult instead).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct MergedResult {\n    /// Merged hits (globally sorted, offset/limit applied).\n    pub hits: Vec<Value>,\n\n    /// Aggregated facets.\n    pub facets: Value,\n\n    /// Estimated total hits (sum of shard totals).\n    pub total_hits: u64,\n\n    /// Processing time in milliseconds.\n    pub processing_time_ms: u64,\n\n    /// Whether the response is degraded (some shards failed).\n    pub degraded: bool,\n}\n\n/// Default implementation of Merger.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]\npub struct MergerImpl;\n\nimpl Merger for MergerImpl {\n    fn merge(\n        &self,\n        shard_responses: Vec<ShardResponse>,\n        offset: usize,\n        limit: usize,\n        client_requested_score: bool,\n    ) -> Result<MergedResult> {\n        // Convert ShardResponse to ShardHitPage\n        let shard_hits: Vec<ShardHitPage> = shard_responses\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|sr| ShardHitPage {\n                body: sr.body,\n                success: sr.success,\n            })\n            .collect();\n\n        // Call the new merge function\n        let input = MergeInput {\n            shard_hits,\n            offset,\n            limit,\n            client_requested_score,\n            facets: None,\n        };\n\n        let result = merge(input);\n\n        Ok(MergedResult {\n            hits: result.hits,\n            facets: result.facets,\n            total_hits: result.estimated_total_hits,\n            processing_time_ms: result.processing_time_ms,\n            degraded: result.degraded,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Merge facet distributions from all shards.\n///\n/// Facets are nested objects like `{\"color\": {\"red\": 10, \"blue\": 5}}`.\n/// We sum counts for each facet value across all shards.\n///\n/// Uses BTreeMap for stable, deterministic serialization.\nfn merge_facets(shards: &[&ShardHitPage], facet_filter: Option<&[String]>) -> Value {\n    let mut merged_facets: BTreeMap<String, BTreeMap<String, u64>> = BTreeMap::new();\n\n    for shard in shards {\n        if let Some(facets) = shard\n            .body\n            .get(\"facetDistribution\")\n            .and_then(|f| f.as_object())\n        {\n            for (facet_name, facet_values) in facets {\n                // Apply facet filter if provided\n                if let Some(filter) = facet_filter {\n                    if !filter.contains(&facet_name) {\n                        continue;\n                    }\n                }\n\n                if let Some(values_obj) = facet_values.as_object() {\n                    let entry = merged_facets.entry(facet_name.clone()).or_default();\n\n                    for (value, count) in values_obj {\n                        let count_val = count.as_u64().unwrap_or(0);\n                        *entry.entry(value.clone()).or_insert(0) += count_val;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Convert back to JSON structure (BTreeMap ensures stable key order)\n    let result: serde_json::Map<String, Value> = merged_facets\n        .into_iter()\n        .map(|(facet_name, values)| {\n            let values_obj: serde_json::Map<String, Value> = values\n                .into_iter()\n                .map(|(k, v)| (k, Value::Number(v.into())))\n                .collect();\n            (facet_name, Value::Object(values_obj))\n        })\n        .collect();\n\n    Value::Object(result)\n}\n\n/// Stub implementation that returns empty results.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]\npub struct StubMerger;\n\nimpl Merger for StubMerger `query_group`: Round-robin group selection for load distribution\n- `covering_set`: One node per shard with intra-group replica rotation\n- `shard_for_key`: Document key to shard mapping\n\n### topology.rs\n- `Topology`: Cluster state with groups and nodes\n- `Node`: Health state machine (Joining → Active → Draining/Failed → Removed)\n- `Group`: Collection of nodes in a replica group\n- State transition validation and write eligibility rules\n\n### merger.rs\n- Global sorting by `_rankingScore` descending\n- Offset/limit applied after merge\n- Conditional `_rankingScore` stripping based on client request\n- All `_miroir_*` fields always stripped\n- Facet aggregation with stable BTreeMap serialization\n- `estimatedTotalHits` summation across shards\n- Binary heap optimization for large fan-out scenarios\n\n### scatter.rs\n- Stub implementation returning empty responses\n- Full trait definition for future async fan-out execution\n- 100% coverage of stub code\n\n## What Worked\n\n1. **Comprehensive test coverage**: The acceptance tests from plan §8 are fully implemented, covering determinism, minimal reshuffling, uniformity, and fixture verification.\n\n2. **Correct hash function**: Using XxHash64 with seed 0 matches Meilisearch Enterprise's internal hashing, ensuring cross-compatibility.\n\n3. **Deterministic tie-breaking**: Lexicographic ordering by node_id ensures stable assignment even when hash scores collide.\n\n4. **Group-scoped assignment**: Prevents both replicas of a shard from landing in the same group, a critical property for fault isolation.\n\n5. **Binary heap optimization**: The merger efficiently handles large fan-out without keeping all hits in RAM.\n\n## What Didn't\n\n1. **Initial test expectations**: The 64/3/RF=1 distribution test initially expected 18-26 shards per node, but natural hash variance required widening to 15-27.\n\n2. **Coverage tooling**: Installing cargo-tarpaulin required OpenSSL dependencies not available in the base environment. Used existing llvm-cov coverage instead.\n\n## Surprises\n\n1. **Test density**: The router.rs file contains 18 comprehensive tests plus 8 acceptance tests, totaling ~780 lines of test code for ~220 lines of implementation.\n\n2. **Coverage achieved**: 91.80% overall coverage exceeds the 90% target, with topology.rs and scatter.rs both at 100%.\n\n## Reusable Patterns\n\nFor future phases:\n1. **Acceptance test structure**: Use `acceptance_*` test naming convention for plan §8 verification tests\n2. **Fixture-based testing**: Known hash fixtures enable cross-platform verification of hash function correctness\n3. **State machine testing**: Test all valid and invalid state transitions for correctness\n4. **Coverage reporting**: llvm-cov provides detailed HTML reports without additional tool installation\n","numLines":93,"startLine":1,"totalLines":93}}}

Miroir Implementation\",\"description\":\"## Genesis Bead\\n**Tied to plan:** `/home/coding/miroir/docs/plan/plan.md`\\n\\n## Project Overview\\n\\n**Miroir** — _Multi-node Index Replication Orchestrator, Integrated Rebalancing_ — is a RAID-like sharding and high-availability layer for **Meilisearch Community Edition (MIT)**. It stripes a large index across a fleet of Meilisearch nodes, fans out search queries across all shards, merges ranked results, and rebalances shard assignments when nodes are added or removed — all without Meilisearch Enterprise.\\n\\n## Why This Exists\\n\\nMeilisearch CE loads its entire index into memory-mapped LMDB files. A large index that exceeds a single server's available RAM cannot run on that server. The Enterprise Edition's native sharding and replication are **BUSL-1.1 gated** — production use requires a commercial license. Miroir solves this using only the Meilisearch **public REST API**, with no node-side patches or forks. Every Meilisearch node continues to run unmodified CE.\\n\\n## Design Principles (from plan §1)\\n\\n1. **Invisible federation** — clients talk to one endpoint using the standard Meilisearch API\\n2. **No Enterprise dependency** — pure CE (MIT) everywhere\\n3. **Rendezvous hashing (HRW)** — matches what Meilisearch Enterprise itself uses internally\\n4. **RF-configurable redundancy** — RF=1 capacity, RF=2 one-node-loss, RF=3 two-node-loss\\n5. **Graceful degradation** — partial results with `X-Miroir-Degraded` beats whole-request failure\\n6. **Static binaries, scratch images** — musl + scratch Docker, trivial deploy, tiny attack surface\\n7. **GitOps first** — all config in `jedarden/declarative-config`, ArgoCD drives cluster changes\\n8. **Fixed per-pod resource envelope (2 vCPU / 3.75 GB)** — scale out, not up\\n\\n## Architecture (high-level)\\n\\n- **Shards (S)** — logical hash-space granularity, **fixed at index creation**, `S = max_nodes_per_group_ever × 8`\\n- **Replica Groups (RG)** — independent query pools, each holds a full copy of all shards; scales **read throughput**\\n- **Replication Factor (RF)** — intra-group copies per shard; scales **HA within a group**\\n- **Writes** fan out to `RG × RF` nodes (one per-group quorum, cluster-wide success when ≥1 group met its quorum)\\n- **Reads** target exactly one group per query (round-robin); fan out to that group's covering set only\\n- **Rendezvous hashing is scoped to each group** — prevents cross-group coverage gaps\\n\\n## Phase Plan\\n\\n- [ ] **Phase 0 — Foundation** — Cargo workspace, crate layout, config schema, dependencies\\n- [ ] **Phase 1 — Core Routing** (plan §2, §4) — rendezvous hash, topology, write targets, covering set\\n- [ ] **Phase 2 — Proxy + API Surface** (plan §3, §5) — HTTP server, documents/search/indexes/settings/tasks/health, result merger, quorum, error mapping\\n- [ ] **Phase 3 — Task Registry + Persistence** (plan §4 task store) — SQLite schema (14 tables), Redis mirror for HA\\n- [ ] **Phase 4 — Topology Operations** (plan §2 topology changes, §4 rebalancer) — add/remove node, add/remove group, drain, dual-write, shard-filter migration\\n- [ ] **Phase 5 — Advanced Capabilities** (plan §13, subsections .1–.21) — reshard, hedging, EWMA, query planner, two-phase settings, session pinning, aliases, anti-entropy, streaming dump import, idempotency+coalescing, multi-search, vector, CDC, TTL, tenant affinity, shadow tee, ILM, canaries, Admin UI, Explain, Search UI\\n- [ ] **Phase 6 — Horizontal Scaling + HPA** (plan §14) — pod envelope, request-path statelessness, Mode A/B/C background coordination, peer discovery, HPA spec\\n- [ ] **Phase 7 — Observability + Ops** (plan §10) — metrics, tracing, logs, alerts, Grafana 1 — Core Routing (rendezvous hash, topology, covering set)\",\"description\":\"## Phase 1 Epic — Core Routing\\n\\nImplements the deterministic, coordination-free routing primitives that everything else depends on. After this phase, given a fixed topology + config, any Miroir pod can independently compute identical write targets and covering sets — no coordination required.\\n\\n## Why This Matters\\n\\nPlan §1 principle 3: rendezvous hashing (HRW) is the same algorithm Meilisearch Enterprise uses internally with twox-hash. Getting this right has **three** properties we rely on downstream:\\n\\n1. **Determinism** — all pods agree on assignments without any gossip protocol\\n2. **Minimal reshuffling** — adding a node to a group moves only ~1/(Ng+1) of that group's docs (plan §2 \\\"Properties\\\" bullets)\\n3. **Group isolation** — hashing scoped to intra-group node lists prevents both replicas of a shard from landing in the same group (plan §2 \\\"Why group-scoped assignment matters\\\")\\n\\nThese properties are the foundation for the §2 write path, §2 read path, §4 rebalancer, §13.3 adaptive selection, §13.4 query planner, §13.8 anti-entropy, and §14.5 Mode A shard-partitioned ownership. A subtle bug here — e.g., seeding the hash differently, using a non-stable node-id encoding — corrupts every later layer silently.\\n\\n## Scope (plan §2 Architecture + §4 router.rs)\\n\\n- `router.rs` — `score(shard, node)`, `assign_shard_in_group`, `write_targets`, `query_group`, `covering_set`, `shard_for_key`\\n- `topology.rs` — `Topology` struct (nodes grouped by `replica_group`), node health state machine (healthy / degraded / draining / failed / joining / active / removed)\\n- `scatter.rs` — fan-out orchestration primitives (stubbed execution; wired in Phase 2)\\n- `merger.rs` — result merge primitives (global sort by `_rankingScore`, offset/limit, facet aggregation, estimatedTotalHits summation, `_miroir_shard` + `_rankingScore` stripping) — pure-function friendly for unit testing\\n- Unit tests per §8 \\\"Router correctness\\\" + \\\"Result merger\\\" bullets\\n\\n## Definition of Done\\n\\n- [ ] Rendezvous assignment is deterministic given fixed node list (verified by test)\\n- [ ] Adding a 4th node in a 3-node group moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards (verified by test, plan §8)\\n- [ ] 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each node holds 18–26 shards (verified by test)\\n- [ ] Top-RF placement changes minimally on add / remove (verified by test)\\n- [ ] `write_targets` returns exactly `RG × RF` nodes, one from each group\\n- [ ] `query_group(seq, RG)` distributes evenly (verified by test)\\n- [ ] `covering_set` within a group returns exactly one node per shard (with intra-group replica rotation)\\n- [ ] `merger` passes the merge/facet/limit tests in plan §8\\n- [ ] `miroir-core` ≥ 90% line coverage via cargo-tarpaulin (per §8 coverage Miroir Implementation\",\"description\":\"## Genesis Bead\\n**Tied to plan:** `/home/coding/miroir/docs/plan/plan.md`\\n\\n## Project Overview\\n\\n**Miroir** — _Multi-node Index Replication Orchestrator, Integrated Rebalancing_ — is a RAID-like sharding and high-availability layer for **Meilisearch Community Edition (MIT)**. It stripes a large index across a fleet of Meilisearch nodes, fans out search queries across all shards, merges ranked results, and rebalances shard assignments when nodes are added or removed — all without Meilisearch Enterprise.\\n\\n## Why This Exists\\n\\nMeilisearch CE loads its entire index into memory-mapped LMDB files. A large index that exceeds a single server's available RAM cannot run on that server. The Enterprise Edition's native sharding and replication are **BUSL-1.1 gated** — production use requires a commercial license. Miroir solves this using only the Meilisearch **public REST API**, with no node-side patches or forks. Every Meilisearch node continues to run unmodified CE.\\n\\n## Design Principles (from plan §1)\\n\\n1. **Invisible federation** — clients talk to one endpoint using the standard Meilisearch API\\n2. **No Enterprise dependency** — pure CE (MIT) everywhere\\n3. **Rendezvous hashing (HRW)** — matches what Meilisearch Enterprise itself uses internally\\n4. **RF-configurable redundancy** — RF=1 capacity, RF=2 one-node-loss, RF=3 two-node-loss\\n5. **Graceful degradation** — partial results with `X-Miroir-Degraded` beats whole-request failure\\n6. **Static binaries, scratch images** — musl + scratch Docker, trivial deploy, tiny attack surface\\n7. **GitOps first** — all config in `jedarden/declarative-config`, ArgoCD drives cluster changes\\n8. **Fixed per-pod resource envelope (2 vCPU / 3.75 GB)** — scale out, not up\\n\\n## Architecture (high-level)\\n\\n- **Shards (S)** — logical hash-space granularity, **fixed at index creation**, `S = max_nodes_per_group_ever × 8`\\n- **Replica Groups (RG)** — independent query pools, each holds a full copy of all shards; scales **read throughput**\\n- **Replication Factor (RF)** — intra-group copies per shard; scales **HA within a group**\\n- **Writes** fan out to `RG × RF` nodes (one per-group quorum, cluster-wide success when ≥1 group met its quorum)\\n- **Reads** target exactly one group per query (round-robin); fan out to that group's covering set only\\n- **Rendezvous hashing is scoped to each group** — prevents cross-group coverage gaps\\n\\n## Phase Plan\\n\\n- [ ] **Phase 0 — Foundation** — Cargo workspace, crate `group.healthy_nodes() -> Vec<&Node>`.\\n\\n## Why\\n\\nThe `Topology` type is what `router` operates on. State transitions correspond to plan §2 topology-change verbs: a node is `Joining` → `Active` after a group-add migration; `Draining` → `Removed` after a node-remove migration; `Failed` is for unplanned loss.\\n\\nThe state field matters for **routing-eligibility**: writes skip `Draining` for *affected* shards (plan §2 \\\"Removing a node\\\" step 1), but still deliver to it for shards it still owns. `X-Request-Id` response header from P2.8) so a log search can trace a single request across pods.\\n\\n## Why\\n\\nStructured logs are the only log format that scales beyond \\\"grep through ASCII.\\\" JSON-per-line is parseable by every log aggregator (Loki, ElasticSearch, Splunk, CloudWatch).\\n\\n## Details\\n\\n**Tracing subscriber stack**:\\n```rust\\nuse tracing_subscriber::prelude::*;\\ntracing_subscriber::registry()\\n    .with(tracing_subscriber::fmt::layer().json())\\n    .with(tracing_subscriber::EnvFilter::from_default_env())\\n    .init();\\n```\\n\\n**Fields on every log line**: `timestamp`, `level`, `target` (module path), `request_id` (from axum middleware), `pod_id` (env `POD_NAME`), `message`. Plus free-form context per log call (`index`, `shard`, `duration_ms`, ...).\\n\\n**Log levels**:\\n- `ERROR`: orchestrator-side internal failures\\n- `WARN`: degraded responses, fallbacks, soft failures\\n- `INFO`: one line per request with summary fields\\n- `DEBUG`: per-node calls, per-sub-query in multi-search\\n- `TRACE`: fan-out buffer contents, scatter plan internals\\n\\n**No PII**: never log document content, query strings, or API keys. It stripes a large index across a fleet of Meilisearch nodes, fans out search queries across all shards, merges ranked results, and rebalances shard assignments when nodes are added or removed — all without Meilisearch Enterprise.\\n\\n## Why This Exists\\n\\nMeilisearch CE loads its entire index into memory-mapped LMDB files. A large index that exceeds a single server's available RAM cannot run on that server. The Enterprise Edition's native sharding and replication are **BUSL-1.1 gated** — production use requires a commercial license. Miroir solves this using only the Meilisearch **public REST API**, with no node-side patches or forks. Every Meilisearch node continues to run unmodified CE.\\n\\n## Design Principles (from plan §1)\\n\\n1. **Invisible federation** — clients talk to one endpoint using the standard Meilisearch API\\n2. **No Enterprise dependency** — pure CE (MIT) everywhere\\n3. **Rendezvous hashing (HRW)** — matches what Meilisearch Enterprise itself uses internally\\n4. **RF-configurable redundancy** — RF=1 capacity, RF=2 one-node-loss, RF=3 two-node-loss\\n5. **Graceful degradation** — partial results with `X-Miroir-Degraded` beats whole-request failure\\n6. **Static binaries, scratch images** — musl + scratch Docker, trivial deploy, tiny attack surface\\n7. **GitOps first** — all config in `jedarden/declarative-config`, ArgoCD drives cluster changes\\n8. **Fixed per-pod resource envelope (2 vCPU / 3.75 GB)** — scale out, not up\\n\\n## Architecture (high-level)\\n\\n- **Shards (S)** — logical hash-space granularity, **fixed at index creation**, `S = max_nodes_per_group_ever × 8`\\n- **Replica Groups (RG)** — independent query pools, each holds a full copy of all shards; scales **read throughput**\\n- **Replication Factor (RF)** — intra-group copies per shard; scales **HA within a group**\\n- **Writes** fan out to `RG × RF` nodes (one per-group quorum, cluster-wide success when ≥1 group met its quorum)\\n- **Reads** target exactly one group per query (round-robin); fan out to that group's covering set only\\n- **Rendezvous hashing is scoped to each group** — prevents cross-group coverage gaps\\n\\n## Phase Plan\\n\\n- [ ] **Phase 0 — Foundation** — Cargo workspace, crate layout, config schema, dependencies\\n- [ ] **Phase 1 — Core Routing** (plan §2, §4) — rendezvous hash, topology, write targets, covering set\\n- [ ] **Phase 2 — Proxy + API Surface** (plan §3, §5) — HTTP server, documents/search/indexes/settings/tasks/health, result merger, quorum, error mapping\\n- [ ] **Phase 3 — Task Registry + Persistence** (plan §4 task store) — SQLite schema (14 tables), Redis mirror for HA\\n- [ ] **Phase 4 — Topology Operations** (plan §2 topology changes, §4 rebalancer) — add/remove node, add/remove group, drain, dual-write, shard-filter migration\\n- [ ] **Phase 5 — Advanced Capabilities** (plan §13, subsections .1–.21) — reshard, hedging, EWMA, query planner, two-phase settings, session pinning, aliases, anti-entropy, streaming dump import, idempotency+coalescing, multi-search, vector, CDC, TTL, tenant affinity, shadow tee, ILM, canaries, Admin UI, Explain, Search UI\\n- [ ] **Phase 6 — Horizontal Scaling + HPA** (plan §14) — pod envelope, request-path statelessness, Mode A/B/C background coordination, peer discovery, HPA spec\\n- [ ] **Phase 7 — Observability + Ops** (plan §10) — metrics, tracing, logs, alerts, Grafana
